[4:1:344,481] Agency oversees departments, boards,  

[5:0:344,491] commissions, and agencies that: protect the  

[5:1:344,501] public through the licensing and regulation of  

[5:2:344,511] more than 100 businesses and 200 professional  

[5:3:344,520] categories; regulate financial services and state-

[5:4:344,530] licensed financial institutions; regulate the sale of  

[5:5:344,540] alcoholic beverages; regulate the cannabis  

[5:6:344,550] industry; regulate the horse racing industry;  

[5:7:344,560] investigate and prosecute civil rights violations;  

[5:8:344,570] and promote safe and affordable housing  

[6:0:344,580] opportunities. The Agency is comprised of the  

[6:1:344,590] following entities: the Departments of Alcoholic  

[6:2:344,600] Beverage Control, Cannabis Control, Consumer  

[6:3:344,610] Affairs, Fair Employment and Housing, Financial  

[6:4:344,619] Protection and Innovation, Housing and  

[7:0:344,629] Community Development, and Real Estate; the  

[7:1:344,639] California Housing Finance Agency; the Alcoholic  

[7:2:344,649] Beverage Control Appeals Board; the California  

[7:3:344,659] Horse Racing Board; the Cannabis Control  

[7:4:344,669] Appeals Panel; and the Homeless Coordinating  

[7:5:344,679] and Financing Council, which serves as a  

[7:6:344,689] statewide facilitator, coordinator, and policy  

[8:0:344,699] development resource to address homelessness.

[1:0:194,39] 1045   Cannabis Control Appeals Panel  

[2:0:66,61] The Cannabis Control Appeals Panel (Panel) was established pursuant to the November 2016 voter approved Proposition 64,  

[2:1:66,71] the Adult Use of Marijuana Act, and amended by Chapter 27, Statutes of 2017 (SB 94), the Medicinal and Adult-Use Cannabis  

[2:2:66,81] Regulation and Safety Act.   The Panel is organized under the Business, Consumer Services and Housing Agency and consists  

[2:3:66,91] of five members, one appointed by the Senate, one appointed by the Assembly, and three appointed by the Governor, subject  

[2:4:66,101] to confirmation by the Senate.  

[3:0:66,122] The Panel provides a forum of appeal for individuals to address licensing decisions made by a cannabis licensing authority  

[3:1:66,132] relating to any penalty assessment, denial, transfer, condition, suspension, revocation, or other disciplinary action of  

[3:2:66,142] annual   cannabis licenses.   The Panel streamlines the appeals process, and provides expertise and due process   in the review  

[3:3:66,152] of licensing decisions.

[10:0:66,571] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[10:1:66,590] 1045 - CANNABIS APPEALS PANEL  

[11:0:66,608] The Cannabis Control Appeals Panel is responsible for appeals from decisions by the Bureau of Cannabis Control, the  

[11:1:66,618] California Department of Public Health, and the California Department of Food Agriculture.   Beginning in 2021-22, the licensing  

[11:2:66,628] functions currently under these entities   are proposed to be consolidated   into a new Department of Cannabis Control.   Decisions  

[11:3:66,638] that may be appealed include ordering penalties, issuing, denying, transferring, conditioning, suspending, or revoking any  

[11:4:66,649] cannabis license provided by the state.

[3:0:195,100] 1111   Department of Consumer Affairs  

[4:0:66,121] The Department of Consumer Affairs (Department) is responsible for promoting and protecting the interests of millions of  

[4:1:66,131] California consumers by serving as a guardian and advocate for their health, safety, and economic well-being and by promoting  

[4:2:66,141] legal and ethical standards of professional conduct. The Department helps promote good business practices and ensure  

[4:3:66,152] California's consumers receive quality services by establishing minimal competency standards for approximately 250  

[5:0:66,162] professions and occupations involving more than three million professionals. The Department is also an important advocate on  

[5:1:66,172] consumer and business issues. In general, the Department's Boards and Bureaus provide exams and licensing, enforcement,  

[5:2:66,182] complaint resolution, and education for consumers.  

[6:0:66,200] In addition, the Department provides centralized services for efficiency. Specifically, Department staff investigate complaints  

[6:1:66,210] against licensees; develop valid examinations for applicants for licensure; monitor and advocate for legislation; provide  

[6:2:66,220] consumer education and outreach; provide legal and audit services; and provide general administrative support involving  

[6:3:66,231] personnel, budgeting, accounting, purchasing, and space management.  

[7:0:66,248] There are currently 26 boards,   one committee, and one commission under the broad authority of the Department, and eight  

[7:1:66,258] bureaus and one certification program under the direct oversight of the Department. The Bureau of Cannabis Control   will be  

[7:2:66,269] consolidated, along with the state’s other cannabis   licensing entities, into the Department of Cannabis Control effective July 1,  

[7:3:66,279] 2021.

[14:0:66,586] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[14:1:65,606] • Consolidation of Cannabis Licensing Entities—The Budget includes the consolidation of the functions and positions of the  

[14:2:76,616] Bureau of Cannabis Control, the Department of Food and Agriculture, and the Department of Public Health into a new stand-

[14:3:76,626] alone Department of Cannabis Control within the Business, Consumer Services, and Housing Agency beginning July 2021.  

[14:4:76,636] This consolidation will simplify participation in the legal market and support the successful and safe operation of cannabis  

[14:5:76,647] businesses in compliance with state law.  

[15:0:65,663] • Local Jurisdiction Assistance Grants—The Budget includes $100   million one-time General Fund in 2021-22 to establish a  

[15:1:76,673] local jurisdiction assistance grant program to help local governments and aid licensees in successfully and swiftly moving  

[15:2:76,683] from provisional licenses into annual licenses, and to do so in a way that supports environmental compliance requirements.  

[15:3:65,699] • Fee Waiver or Deferral Program—The Budget includes $30 million one-time General Fund in 2021-22 to implement a fee  

[15:4:76,710] waiver or deferral program pursuant to the provisions of Chapter 852, Statutes of 2019 (SB 595), to reduce barriers to entry

[8:0:66,709] state’s progress toward higher levels of seismic safety. To support this broad mission, the Commission uses the expertise of its

[3:0:66,69] commissioners to review, evaluate, and translate scientific information and make recommendations to guide and influence  

[3:1:66,79] earthquake safety policies.  

[4:0:66,97] The Commission works with federal, state, and local agencies, as well as the private sector, on a variety of activities that  

[4:1:66,107] support the state’s earthquake preparedness, mitigation, response, and recovery. These activities include: (1) developing and  

[4:2:66,117] reviewing seismic safety projects; (2) providing a consistent policy direction; (3) proposing and reviewing earthquake-related  

[4:3:66,127] legislation; (4) conducting public hearings on seismic safety issues; (5) using existing knowledge and conducting studies,  

[4:4:66,137] where necessary, to improve the performance of structures in California, (6) recommending earthquake safety programs and  

[4:5:66,148] supporting cost-effective partnerships that help reduce earthquake risks and speed economic recovery.  

[4:6:66,165] The Budget reflects the transfer of the Commission to the Office of Emergency Services beginning in 2020-21, consistent with  

[4:7:66,175] Chapter 20, Statutes of 2020 (AB 100).

[10:0:158,376] 1700   Department of Fair Employment and Housing  

[10:1:66,398] The Department of Fair Employment and Housing (Department) is responsible for protecting the civil rights of the people of  

[10:2:66,408] California. The Department receives, investigates, conciliates, mediates, and prosecutes complaints alleging unlawful  

[10:3:66,418] discrimination in employment, housing, and public accommodation, and acts of hate violence and human trafficking. The  

[10:4:66,428] Department is authorized to commence prosecution by filing cases directly in court, and to seek attorney's fees and costs when  

[10:5:66,439] it is the prevailing party. The Department's jurisdiction extends to individuals, private and public entities, housing providers, and  

[10:6:66,449] business establishments within California.  

[11:0:66,469] The Fair Employment and Housing Council (Council) within the Department promulgates regulations interpreting California's  

[11:1:66,479] civil rights laws.

[7:0:66,356] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[7:1:66,375] 1510 - INVESTMENT PROGRAM  

[8:0:66,393] The objective of this program is to protect investors in securities and franchise investment transactions and to promote capital  

[8:1:66,403] formation in California.   The program regulates the offer and sale of certain securities, franchises, and licenses and examines  

[8:2:66,413] broker-dealers and investment advisers.  

[8:3:66,431] 1515 - LENDER-FIDUCIARY PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,451] The objective of this program is to protect consumers who borrow and enter into financial transactions with lenders and  

[9:1:66,461] fiduciaries licensed by the Department.   The program licenses and regulates businesses engaged in financial transactions such  

[9:2:66,472] as mortgage loan originators, finance lenders, escrow agents, deferred deposit originators, bill payers, proraters, securities  

[9:3:66,482] depositories, and property assessed clean energy programs.  

[9:4:66,499] 1520 - LICENSING AND SUPERVISION OF BANKS AND TRUST COMPANIES  

[10:0:66,520] The objective of this program is to promote the integrity and stability of state-licensed banks and trust companies, student loan  

[10:1:66,530] servicing, state-licensed business and industrial development corporations, and state-licensed public banks, industrial banks,  

[10:2:66,540] and premium finance companies.   This objective is achieved through the regulation, supervision, and examination of these  

[10:3:66,550] institutions, which helps to provide their safe and sound operation and compliance with laws and regulations.  

[10:4:66,568] 1525 - MONEY TRANSMITTERS  

[11:0:66,589] The objective of this program is to promote the integrity and stability of businesses that receive money for transmission, and  

[11:1:66,599] sell or issue payment instruments and stored value.   This objective is achieved through the regulation, supervision, and  

[11:2:66,609] examination of these institutions, which helps to provide their safe and sound operation and compliance with laws and

[9:0:182,519] 1703   California Privacy Protection Agency  

[10:0:66,541] Proposition 24, the California Privacy Rights Act of 2020, was approved by California voters on November 3, 2020, creating the  

[10:1:66,551] California Privacy Protection Agency. The Agency is vested with administrative power, authority, and jurisdiction to implement  

[10:2:66,561] and enforce the California Consumer Privacy Act of 2018, which is aimed at protecting the use of personal information and the  

[10:3:66,571] promotion of public awareness and understanding of the risks, rules, and rights related to the collection, use, sale, and  

[10:4:66,581] disclosure of personal information, including the rights of minors.  

[11:0:66,599] The agency is governed by a five-member board, including the chairperson. The chairperson and one member of the board are  

[11:1:66,609] appointed by the Governor. The Attorney General, Senate Rules Committee, and Speaker of the Assembly each appoint one  

[11:2:66,619] member. These appointments are to be made from among Californians with expertise in the areas of privacy, technology, and  

[11:3:66,630] consumer rights.

[10:0:200,500] 1750   California Horse Racing Board  

[10:1:66,521] The California Horse Racing Board regulates parimutuel wagering for the protection of the public and promotes the horse  

[10:2:66,532] racing and breeding industries.  

[11:0:66,552] Jurisdiction and supervision over meetings in California where horse races with wagering on their results are held, and over all  

[11:1:66,562] things having to do with the operation of such meetings, are vested in the seven-member California Horse Racing Board, who  

[11:2:66,572] are appointed by the Governor.   Principal activities of the Board include:  

[11:3:65,590] • Protecting the public's interests.  

[11:4:65,606] • Enforcing laws, rules, and regulations pertaining to horse racing in California.  

[11:5:65,622] • Conducting research to determine the cause and prevention of horse racing accidents and the effects of drug substances on  

[11:6:76,633] horses, and to detect foreign drug substances.  

[11:7:65,649] • Licensing of racing associations and participants in the racing industry.  

[11:8:65,665] • Acting as a quasi-judicial body in matters pertaining to horse racing meets.  

[11:9:65,681] • Encouraging agriculture and the breeding of horses in the state.  

[11:10:65,697] • Collecting the state's lawful share of revenue derived from horse racing meets.  

[11:11:65,714] • Tabulating, analyzing, and publishing statistical racing information.  

[12:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[7:0:66,298] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[7:1:65,317] • Homekey—The Budget includes $2.2 billion one-time Coronavirus Fiscal Recovery Fund and $550 million one-time General  

[7:2:76,327] Fund to fund additional Homekey projects that can be converted and rehabilitated to provide permanent housing for persons  

[7:3:76,337] experiencing homelessness and who are also at risk of COVID-19 or other communicable diseases.  

[7:4:65,353] • Streamlining Backlogged Affordable Housing—The Budget provides $1.75 billion one-time Coronavirus State Fiscal  

[7:5:76,364] Recovery Fund to more than 6,300 shovel ready affordable housing units, which have successfully acquired state funding, to  

[7:6:76,374] expedite the construction of projects in lieu of waiting or applying for state tax credits.  

[7:7:65,390] • Regional Transformative Planning Grants—The Budget includes $600 million one-time funds for HCD to provide additional  

[7:8:76,400] planning and implementation grants to regional entities for transformative planning activities such as infill developments,  

[7:9:76,410] targeted towards the state’s climate goals and reducing vehicle miles traveled.  

[7:10:65,427] • Foreclosure Prevention and Preservation—The Budget appropriates $500 million one-time General Fund to provide loans  

[7:11:76,437] and grants to preserve affordable housing and promote resident ownership or nonprofit organization ownership of homes at  

[7:12:76,447] risk of foreclosure.  

[8:0:65,463] • Preservation Initiative—The Budget includes $300 million one-time Coronavirus Fiscal Recovery Fund to provide capital to  

[8:1:76,473] HCD legacy projects about to go market-rate to extend affordability covenants and preserve the state’s affordable housing  

[8:2:76,484] stock.  

[9:0:65,500] • Homebuyer Assistance—The Budget provides $100 million one-time General Fund to CalHFA’s First Time Homebuyer  

[9:1:76,510] Assistance Program to help prospective homebuyers, particularly in disadvantaged areas, make a down payment, secure a  

[9:2:76,520] loan, and pay closing costs on a home.  

[10:0:65,536] • Accessory Dwelling Unit (ADU) Financing—The Budget includes $81 million one-time Coronavirus State Fiscal Recovery  

[10:1:76,547] Fund to expand CalHFA’s ADU financing program for the construction of new ADUs. This supplements $19 million currently  

[10:2:76,557] appropriated for the program, providing a total $100 million to support low-cost production and increase the number of  

[10:3:76,567] housing units statewide.  

[11:0:65,583] • Mixed Income Housing—The Budget includes $45 million one-time General Fund to CalHFA’s Mixed-Income Program to  

[11:1:76,593] provide loans to developers for new mixed-income housing.  

[12:0:65,610] • Scaling Excess Lands—The Budget provides $45 million one-time Coronavirus State Fiscal Recovery Funds for site  

[12:1:76,620] remediation and local government matching grants to scale up excess land affordable housing development.  

[12:2:65,636] • Infill Infrastructure Grant Program—The Budget provides $250 million one-time General Fund and reallocates $284 in  

[12:3:76,646] remaining Proposition 1 funds for the popular Infill Infrastructure Grant Program. This provides a total $534 million for critical  

[12:4:76,656] infrastructure for affordable housing.  

[13:0:65,673] • Golden State Acquisition Fund—The Budget appropriates $50 million one-time General Fund to the Golden State Acquisition  

[13:1:76,683] Fund, which will be matched by various community development financial institutions in a revolving fund to leverage  

[13:2:76,693] additional capital for acquisition or preservation of affordable housing statewide.  

[13:3:65,709] • Office of Migrant Services-Deferred Maintenance—The Budget provides $30 million one-time General Fund for critical  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[4:0:66,307] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:1:66,326] 1660 - CODES AND STANDARDS PROGRAM  

[5:0:66,344] The objective of this program is to protect the public's health, safety, and general welfare in buildings and structures designed  

[5:1:66,354] for human occupancy through the enforcement of the California Health and Safety Code, including the State Housing Law,  

[5:2:66,364] Employee Housing Act, Mobilehome Parks Act, Special Occupancy Parks Act, California Factory-Built Housing Law, and the  

[5:3:66,375] Mobilehome-Manufactured Housing Act. HCD works with factory and site-built building industries, stakeholders, and other  

[5:4:66,385] government agencies to review and propose the adoption of international, national, and uniform building codes as the basis for  

[5:5:66,395] all residential construction in California. The program also enforces federal and state standards for the construction, safety,  

[5:6:66,405] sales, and titling of manufactured homes, mobilehomes, and commercial modulars.  

[5:7:66,423] 1665 - FINANCIAL ASSISTANCE PROGRAM  

[6:0:66,443] The objectives of this program are to: (1) increase housing supply by providing loans and grants to develop and preserve safe  

[6:1:66,453] and affordable housing for lower-income households, (2) promote economic, community, and job development by awarding  

[6:2:66,464] state and federal housing funds, (3) reduce homelessness through financial assistance and policy leadership, and (4) monitor  

[6:3:66,474] funding recipients for compliance with the terms of their contracts with the state.  

[6:4:66,492] 1670 - HOUSING POLICY DEVELOPMENT PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,512] The objectives of this program are to: (1) facilitate an adequate supply of housing affordable to all income groups through the  

[7:1:66,522] development, promotion, and implementation of innovative housing and community development policies, practices, programs,  

[7:2:66,532] and partnerships with state, regional, and local partners, (2) provide oversight for local housing plans, (3) administer planning  

[7:3:66,543] and incentive grant programs, and (4) provide research, collect and analyze data, and evaluate and communicate progress in  

[7:4:66,553] meeting HCD goals and outcomes.  

[7:5:66,570] 1675 - CALIFORNIA HOUSING FINANCE AGENCY  

[8:0:66,588] CalHFA is statutorily required to maintain financial and operational independence, setting loan interest rates slightly above its  

[8:1:66,598] cost of funds and charging fees to cover its lending costs and risks. The objective of CalHFA's lending activity is to advance the  

[8:2:66,609] creation and preservation of affordable housing using various lending models that facilitate: (1) mortgage loans to qualified low  

[8:3:66,619] and moderate income homebuyers to finance the purchase of an affordable home, (2) permanent loans to create and preserve  

[8:4:66,629] multifamily housing projects for low and moderate income residents, and (3) special needs housing loans to facilitate the  

[8:5:66,639] construction, rehabilitation, and acquisition of housing needed to serve special needs populations.  

[8:6:66,657] 1680 - LOAN REPAYMENTS PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,677] This program displays the estimated loan repayments made under HCD's Financial Assistance Program.  

[9:1:66,695] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION PROGRAM  

[10:0:66,715] This program provides: (1) executive leadership in designing, implementing, and communicating housing programs and

[3:0:66,69] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,88] 1700 - DEPARTMENT OF REAL ESTATE  

[4:0:66,109] The Department of Real Estate ensures that individuals who wish to engage in real estate business and act in the capacity of,  

[4:1:66,119] or advertise as, a real estate broker or salesperson within California meet specified qualifications, and makes sure licensees  

[4:2:66,129] meet minimum education standards and requirements.   The Department investigates the actions of any person acting in the  

[4:3:66,139] capacity of a real estate licensee, performs financial compliance audits of licensees and subdividers, administratively  

[4:4:66,149] prosecutes violations of the Real Estate Law and Subdivided Lands Law, and provides victims of real estate fraud with financial  

[4:5:66,160] recovery per limitations set by statute.   The Department protects the public against fraud and misrepresentation in the sale or  

[4:6:66,170] lease of subdivided land through the issuance of public reports that disclose vital information to prospective purchasers of  

[4:7:66,180] subdivision interests.
